#METABOLOMICS WORKBENCH sara.oneal@duke.edu_20170404_132629 DATATRACK_ID:878 STUDY_ID:ST000589 ANALYSIS_ID:AN000904
VERSION             	1
CREATED_ON             	April 12, 2017, 3:58 pm
#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Methods for improved identification and quantification in GC-MS-based
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	metabolomic profiling of human plasma
PR:PROJECT_TYPE                  	GC-MS non targeted qualitative analysis
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	The field of metabolomics as applied to human disease and health is rapidly
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	expanding. However, studies reporting experiences with quality-control and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	method validation are lacking. In this study, we sought to identify and modify
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	steps in GC-MS-based metabolomic profiling of human plasma that could influence
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolite identification and quantification. Our experimental design included
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	two studies: 1) the limiting-dilution study, which investigated the effects of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	dilution on analyte identification and quantification, and 2) the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	concentration-specific study, which compared the optimal plasma extract volume
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	established in the first study with the volume used in the current institutional
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	protocol. We confirmed that contaminants, concentration, intra- and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	inter-experiment variability are major factors influencing metabolite
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	identification and quantification. In addition, we established methods for
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	improved metabolite identification and quantification, which were summarized to
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	provide recommendations for experimental design of GC-MS-based profiling of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	human plasma.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	Duke University
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Duke Molecular Physiology Institute
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Wang
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Hanghang
PR:ADDRESS                       	300 North Duke Street, Durham, NC, 27701, USA
PR:EMAIL                         	hanghang.wang@duke.edu
PR:PHONE                         	+1 919 884 0025
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	U.S. Department of Health & Human Services, National Institutes of Health (NIH)
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	- T32HL007101; Thoracic Surgery Foundation for Research and Education (TSFRE) -
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	Braunwald Fellowship
#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Effects of dilution on analyte identification and quantification
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	GC-MS non-targeted metabolomic profiling
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	The limiting-dilution study evaluated the effects of sample dilution on the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	ability to identify and quantify analytes in plasma. The study was divided into
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	10 batches with identical experimental design spanning over a 16-day period.
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Each batch consisted of 33 aliquots with 11 different plasma extract volumes (0
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	– 700 µL) corresponding to 11 plasma concentrations repeated three times.
ST:INSTITUTE                     	Duke University
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Duke Molecular Physiology Institute
ST:LAST_NAME                     	Wang
ST:FIRST_NAME                    	Hanghang
ST:ADDRESS                       	300 North Duke Street, Durham, NC, 27701, USA
ST:EMAIL                         	hanghang.wang@duke.edu
ST:PHONE                         	+1 919 884 0025
ST:NUM_GROUPS                    	10

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	Plasma from blood drawn intravenously
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Blood
CO:COLLECTION_METHOD             	IV
CO:ADDITIVES                     	EDTA
CO:BLOOD_SERUM_OR_PLASMA         	Plasma
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	no treatment
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Protein precipitation and drying followed by derivatization via methoxyamine and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	MSTFA
SP:EXTRACTION_METHOD             	Protein precipitation
SP:SAMPLE_DERIVATIZATION         	18 mg/mL methoxyamine hydrochloride in pyridine for 30 min at 50°C, followed by
SP:SAMPLE_DERIVATIZATION         	trimethylsilylation with N-methyl-N- (trimethylsilyl)trifluoroacetamide (MSTFA)
SP:SAMPLE_DERIVATIZATION         	for 30 min at 50°C
SP:SAMPLE_SPIKING                	retention-time-lock internal standard of perdeuterated myristic acid
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	GC/MS methods follow previous studies using a 6890 N GC connected to a 5975B
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	Inert single quadrupole MS (Agilent Technologies, Santa Clara, CA) (Bonikos et
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	al. 1975; Fiehn 2008; Kind et al. 2009). The two wall-coated, open-tubular GC
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	columns connected in series are both from J&W/Agilent (part 122–5512), DB5-MS,
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	15 meters in length, 0.25 mm in diameter, with an 0.25-l m luminal film.
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	Positive ions generated with conventional electron-ionization at 70 eV are
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	scanned broadly from 600 to 50 m/z in the detector throughout the 45 min cycle
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	time.
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE        	GC
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME            	Agilent 6890N GC/Agilent 5975B MSD
CH:COLUMN_NAME                	DB5-MS, 15 m length, 0.25 mm in dia., with an 0.25-l m luminal film
CH:FLOW_RATE                  	2.0 mL/min
CH:TIME_PROGRAM               	initial GC oven temperature of 60°C increased at 10°C/min to a final
CH:TIME_PROGRAM               	temperature of 325°C
